Jamison Brereton

30 (326)
Indra
V─Бmadeva Gautama
24 verses: g─Бyatr─л, except anuс╣гс╣нubh 8, 24, arranged in trcas ╠е
This long hymn, constructed of triplets, begins with a celebration of IndraтАЩs supreme power (vss. 1тАУ3) and ends with a summary of the same (vss. 22тАУ23, with604 IV.30
24 a pendant). In between lies a catalogue of many of IndraтАЩs famous, and not so famous, deedsтАФthough avoiding the most famous of these, the Vala and Vr╠еtra myths (save in the repeated epithet тАЬVr╠еtra-smasher,тАЭ vss. 1, 19, 22). The most detailed treatments are of IndraтАЩs theft of the SunтАЩs wheel (vss. 4тАУ6) and the smash
ing of DawnтАЩs cart (vss. 8тАУ11), myths whose contents are not entirely clear to us, despite regular allusions to them. Both myths are also treated in X.138, and as in that hymn (see introductory remarks there), we see in both myths a reflection of IndraтАЩs assertion of control over cosmic time by deregulating it, at least temporar
ily. This theme seems to be announced in verse 3c, immediately preceding the story of the SunтАЩs wheel.
The other deeds are related in cursory fashion, one per verse, and the abundance of forms of ut├б тАЬandтАЭ emphasizes the additive nature of the hymn, especially in its second part. In this it resembles the catalogue hymns devoted to the A┼ЫvinsтАЩ rescues and favors to men.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Altogether do the peoples turn, like wheels, following all things that are yours.
Altogether are you famed as great.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Geldner takes v├н┼Ыv─Б with kс╣Ыс╣гс╣н├бyaс╕е, but in this sandhi situation it would have to represent a corruption of v├н┼Ыv─Б┼Ы. See Oldenberg for disc. of this form. I take it as a neut. acc. pl.

Thou ever art renowned as Great.

English translation:

тАЬVerily all the gods, with you (for) their strength, have warred (with the asuras); wherefore you have destroyed by day and by night.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Not even all the gods (altogether) fought you, Indra, because of this: that by night you passed over the days.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The neg. scope problem potentially posed by v├н┼Ыve тАж n├б – тАЬall did notтАЭ vs. тАЬnot all didтАЭ – can be easily solved. See my 1997 тАЬVedic any├б- ‘another, the other’: syntactic disambiguation,тАЭ where I establish that the independent negative n├б coocurs with v├н┼Ыva- only with the corporate entity v├н┼Ыve dev─Б╠Бс╕е, enforcing a meaning тАЬall did not.тАЭ Reading *y┼лyudhuс╕е would provide a better cadence. Oldenberg tentatively endorses this.

The sense of p─Бda c is not entirely clear, but there are several factors that allow us to close in on the meaning. First, it seems to provide the reason why the gods did not fight Indra. Further, ─Б╠Бtiraс╕е recurs in vs. 7, and it seems unlikely that the two identical verbs would have substantially different meanings. Finally, as far as I can tell, all occurrences of n├бktam are temporal (тАШby nightтАЩ); when poets want to refer to night as an entity or entities they use r─Б╠Бtr─л-, akt├║-, or kс╣г├бp-. (On uс╣г─Б╠Бs─Б n├бktam in VIII.27.2, see comm. ad loc.) Therefore tr. like Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) that take ├бh─Б n├бktam as parallel objects (e.g., Geldner тАЬals du Tage und Nacht abgrenztestтАЭ) cannot be correct. As indicated in the published introduction, I think that this p─Бda concerns IndraтАЩs destabilization of time when he steals the SunтАЩs wheel – a myth that will be glancingly related in the next tс╣Ыca. What exactly is going on I donтАЩt know – it sounds as if Indra fast-forwards or skips over days during the night, perhaps because the Sun canтАЩt make his normal daily circuit and therefore daytime is significantly abbreviated and no longer lasts as long as night?

When you fought the swaggering gods, all of them, even though you were alone,

Jamison Brereton Notes

In b I read ─Б╠Бh─Б not ─Б╠Бh─Б (a change only in the Pp. not the Saс╣Гhit─Б text), and analyze this sequence as ─Б╠Б+ ├бh─Б, the neut. pl. of тАШdayтАЩ (found also in IV.30.3 and 33.6; cf. also vi┼Ыv├бh─Б in 12a below). This is one of only two supposed exx. of the particle ha with long vowel; the other one (V.41.7) also follows ─Б╠Бand is susceptible to the same analysis. The ─Б-final version of ha is gh─Б, which shows Brugmann’s Law and velar outcome before original *o, acdg. to Mark Hale. Note that ha only once elsewhere occurs after the preverb ─Б╠Б(VIII.9.18 ─Б╠Бh─Бy├бm тАж). (In fact an analysis ─Б╠Бh─Б╠Бy├бm тАЬthis one through the days here тАжтАЭ is also possible in VIII.9.18, though I did not so analyze it there.) By contrast gh─Б is found fairly commonly after ─Б╠Б(I.30.8, I.48.5, etc.).

тАЬAlong the slope of your intentionsтАЭ (prav├бt─Б тАж kr├бt┼лn─Бm) means that the journey to our sacrifice is an easy one because it is in accord with IndraтАЩs intentions.

Why this should be like coming by foot (pad├йva) is not entirely clear: the journey is so easy that it can be undertaken on foot? pleasant pedestrian rambles generally involve taking an easy downward path? Neither of these seems particular applicable to IndraтАЩs travels.

When s├бc─Б occurs with a loc., it generally lacks lexical value and simply signals a locative absolute – as in the common expression sut├й s├бc─Б тАЬwhen (the soma) is pressed.тАЭ I think that is the intention here, in the phrase s┼л╠Бrye s├бc─Б: it is a temporal expression, тАЬwhen the sun (rises)тАЭ; cf. I.135.3 and comm. ad loc. I have here included a lexical tr. тАЬin company withтАЭ because I think s├бc─Б, with lexical value, needs to be supplied or understood in the next vs., 6c, for which see disc. below.

However, I would now be inclined simply to tr. here тАЬI have taken my share at sun(rise).тАЭ

All three vss. of this tс╣Ыca begin with y├бtra. I take them all as subordinated to vs. 3. Geldner [/Witzel Got┼Н] and Klein (DGRV I.432) take the main clause for all three vss. to be 6c, but IndraтАЩs help for Eta┼Ыa does not seem sufficiently significant to carry the whole tс╣Ыca. Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) take all three y├бtra as тАШwhereтАЩ, not тАШwhenтАЩ, but what location they are thinking of I donтАЩt know.

I do not know what to do with the ut├бтАЩs in y├бtrot├б in 4 and 6, but assume they are there to indicate the additive nature of the sequence of subordinate clauses. Sim.

Klein (DGRV I.431-32). It would be better if the first one were in vs. 5, not vs. 4.

English translation:

тАЬIn which (contests), Indra you have, for the sake of a mortal, discomfited the sun, and have protected Eta┼Ыa by (your) exploits.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

And when for the mortal you let the Sun slip,
and you helped Eta┼Ыa through your powers.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The purport of this verse is something of a puzzle. I think the point is that the journey undertaken by Indra in vs. 4 has finally brought him here, with both his battle-lust and his equipment on full display, in order to drink soma with the ritualists (including the тАЬIтАЭ of the speaker). Cf. nearby IV.29.2, where Indra presents himself in a non-intimidating way (or so he thinks) and тАЬbecomes exhilarated along with the heroes who have pressed the soma.тАЭ Here his arrival is at sunrise, and тАЬIтАЭ have a share in the soma along with Indra at that time. In order to make sense of 6c, we need to understand/supply ├бbhakс╣гi from 5c (as Geldner [/Witzel Got┼Н] do also). Although Klein (DGRV II.129) thinks the two ├бdhaтАЩs in c have different functions, the pointed parallel structure of that short p─Бda – ├бdha LOC ├бdha LOC – makes that conclusion quite unlikely in its strong form – though I think it is the case that the formal parallelism conceals a functional distinction (different from the one suggested by Klein). The question is how to construe the locatives, and it is here that the s├бc─Б in 5c comes into play. As I noted apropos of that p─Бda, the s├бc─Б there seems just to signal that the loc. s┼л╠Бrye is a functional loc. absol. In our p─Бda c there is no s├бc─Б, but I think it should be understood. On the one hand, it again (silently) marks s┼л╠Бrye as a loc. absol.; however, with ├нndre I suggest it has lexical value (as it likely has in the two occurrences of tv├й s├бc─Б in the next hymn [IV.32.3c, 4a]), indicating that тАЬIтАЭ take my share in IndraтАЩs company. What I am suggesting is that a non-overt s├бc─Б, supplied on the basis of its occurrence in the previous vs., has two different functions in a single p─Бda, a p─Бda whose structure suggests that its parts should be rigidly parallel. This is not sufficiently conveyed by the published translation – I am not sure that English is up to conveying it – which I would now emend to тАЬ(I have taken my share) now in (company with) you, now in (company with) the sun (i.e., at sunrise).тАЭ

Jamison Brereton Notes

All three vss. of this tс╣Ыca begin with y├бtra. I take them all as subordinated to vs. 3. Geldner [/Witzel Got┼Н] and Klein (DGRV I.432) take the main clause for all three vss. to be 6c, but IndraтАЩs help for Eta┼Ыa does not seem sufficiently significant to carry the whole tс╣Ыca. Geldner (/Witzel Got┼Н) take all three y├бtra as тАШwhereтАЩ, not тАШwhenтАЩ, but what location they are thinking of I donтАЩt know.

I do not know what to do with the ut├бтАЩs in y├бtrot├б in 4 and 6, but assume they are there to indicate the additive nature of the sequence of subordinate clauses. Sim.

Klein (DGRV I.431-32). It would be better if the first one were in vs. 5, not vs. 4.

Jamison Brereton Notes

In c ├бtra seems to correspond to the three y├бtraтАЩs in the preceding tс╣Ыca. The point seems to be that even after all the energy Indra expended in his fight with the sun (and the gods), he still has a lot of many├║- left to apply in the Uс╣гas incident.

The repetition of ─Б╠Бtiraс╕е here was already noted ad vs. 3. Note the similarity of the p─Бdas: 3c (y├бd) ├бh─Б тАж ─Б╠Бtiraс╕е / 7c (├бtr)─Б╠Бha тАж ─Б╠Бtiraс╕е; though ├бh─Б тАШdaysтАЩ in 3 and the particle ├бha in 7 are unrelated, the echo is surely deliberate.

I supply тАЬlying thereтАЭ with D─Бnu, because in two of the four singular passages containing d─Б╠Бnu- what the D─Бnu does is тАШlieтАЩ: I.32.9 d─Б╠Бnuс╕е ┼Ыaye; II.12.11 d─Б╠Бnuс╣Г ┼Ы├бy─Бnam. So, although тАШovercameтАЩ is probably part of the semantics of ─Б╠Бtiraс╕е, the lit.

sense тАШpass overтАЩ fits having the prostrate enemy as the object.

Jamison Brereton Notes

My interpr. of the structural relationship of these two vss. and of the internal structure of vs. 8 differs considerably from the standard. Because of the parallelism of the openings of these vss., both with ut├б sm─Б, I think that there should be two parallel clauses. But vs. 7 is a h├н clauses with accented verb (─Бh├║с╕е), whereas the only verb in vs. 8 is maс╣Гhase in p─Бda c. I am also puzzled by the p├бri in 8a, which is difficult to construe with the rest. There is no p├бri тИЪmaс╣Гh elsewhere, and p├бri is in any case not situated where we would expect a preverb in tmesis. Witzel Got┼Н tr.

valiantly тАЬdu schenkst тАж ringsum,тАЭ which works in a pinch but I find it unsatisfying.

I suggest instead that p─Бda a contains an abbreviated form of a common formula containing both p├бri and s├бdyaс╕е and a verb of motion. Cf. in IV: nearby IV.33.1 p├бri dy─Б╠Бс╣Г sady├│ ap├бso babh┼лvuс╕е; IV.45.7 y├йna sady├бс╕е p├бri r├бj─Бс╣Гsi y─Бth├бс╕е; IV.51.5 paripray─Бth├б bh├║van─Бni sady├бс╕е. And elsewhere, e.g., I.115.3 p├бri dy─Б╠Бv─Бprthiv ╠е ─л╠Бyanti sady├бс╕е; I.123.8 ├йkaik─Б kr├бtum p├бri yanti sady├бс╕е; I.128.3 ├йvena sady├бс╕е p├бry eti p─Б╠Бrthivam; III.58.8 p├бri dy─Б╠Бv─Бprthiv ╠е ─л╠Бy─Бti sady├бс╕е; V.47.4 div├б┼Ы caranti p├бri sady├│ ├бnt─Бn; VII.5.7 v─Бy├║r n├б p─Б╠Бthaс╕е p├бri p─Бsi sady├бс╕е; VII.75.4 p├б├▒ca kс╣гit─л╠Бс╕е p├бri sady├│ jig─Бti. Given the remarkable number of such collocations, I find it difficult to believe that our poet is not evoking this formula. Since much of this hymn concerns IndraтАЩs journey, it would be contextually appropriate. That vs. 9 asserts that no hindrances can obstruct Indra supports the journey theme. Then, by my interpr., p─Бdas bc constitute the main clause for vss. 7-8.

English translation:

тАЬInasmuch, Indra, as you have displayed such manly prowess, you have slain the woman, the daughter of the sky, when meditating mischief.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The daughter of the sky: the dawn, extinguished by the ascendancy of Indra throughout the day

Jamison Brereton

And you performed this manly and masculine deed, Indra:
that you smote a woman, the evilly angry daughter of Heaven.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The juxtaposition of v─лry├бm тАж pa├║с╣Гsyam тАЬmanly and masculineтАЭ with str├нyam тАЬwomanтАЭ brings the gender polarization into sharp relief. There is certainly no sense that itтАЩs unseemly or unsporting to hit a girl!

Jamison Brereton Notes

My interpr. of the structural relationship of these two vss. and of the internal structure of vs. 8 differs considerably from the standard. Because of the parallelism of the openings of these vss., both with ut├б sm─Б, I think that there should be two parallel clauses. But vs. 7 is a h├н clauses with accented verb (─Бh├║с╕е), whereas the only verb in vs. 8 is maс╣Гhase in p─Бda c. I am also puzzled by the p├бri in 8a, which is difficult to construe with the rest. There is no p├бri тИЪmaс╣Гh elsewhere, and p├бri is in any case not situated where we would expect a preverb in tmesis. Witzel Got┼Н tr.

valiantly тАЬdu schenkst тАж ringsum,тАЭ which works in a pinch but I find it unsatisfying.

I suggest instead that p─Бda a contains an abbreviated form of a common formula containing both p├бri and s├бdyaс╕е and a verb of motion. Cf. in IV: nearby IV.33.1 p├бri dy─Б╠Бс╣Г sady├│ ap├бso babh┼лvuс╕е; IV.45.7 y├йna sady├бс╕е p├бri r├бj─Бс╣Гsi y─Бth├бс╕е; IV.51.5 paripray─Бth├б bh├║van─Бni sady├бс╕е. And elsewhere, e.g., I.115.3 p├бri dy─Б╠Бv─Бprthiv ╠е ─л╠Бyanti sady├бс╕е; I.123.8 ├йkaik─Б kr├бtum p├бri yanti sady├бс╕е; I.128.3 ├йvena sady├бс╕е p├бry eti p─Б╠Бrthivam; III.58.8 p├бri dy─Б╠Бv─Бprthiv ╠е ─л╠Бy─Бti sady├бс╕е; V.47.4 div├б┼Ы caranti p├бri sady├│ ├бnt─Бn; VII.5.7 v─Бy├║r n├б p─Б╠Бthaс╕е p├бri p─Бsi sady├бс╕е; VII.75.4 p├б├▒ca kс╣гit─л╠Бс╕е p├бri sady├│ jig─Бti. Given the remarkable number of such collocations, I find it difficult to believe that our poet is not evoking this formula. Since much of this hymn concerns IndraтАЩs journey, it would be contextually appropriate. That vs. 9 asserts that no hindrances can obstruct Indra supports the journey theme. Then, by my interpr., p─Бdas bc constitute the main clause for vss. 7-8.

English translation:

тАЬThen her shattered wagon reposed (on the bank) of the Vip─Бs’ (river), and she departed from afar.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

This cart of hers lies, very completely crushed, here at the Vip─Б┼Ы (River). She has run into the far distance.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The published translation rather carelessly followed GeldnerтАЩs тАЬzu grossem, glanzvollem Besitz,тАЭ but mah├бс╕е is of course not a dat. like r─Бy├й div├нtmate. It should either be rendered as a gen./abl. of m├бh-, hence тАЬfor the heavenly wealth of/from a/the great oneтАЭ (so, e.g., tentatively Scarlatta 45), or as the adv. mah├бс╕е (see esp. Oldenberg, Kl. Schr. 729- 30 [=ZDMG (1901): 270-71] on mah├│ r─Бy├й), hence тАЬgreatly for heavenly wealth.тАЭ As Oldenberg points out, this phrase is very similar to V.79.1 mah├й тАж r─Бy├й div├нtmat─л, with a real dative mah├й. The purport of the two expressions is probably the same. I would now follow OldenbergтАЩs adverbial interpr. Indeed this very phrase is found a number of times: IV.31.11, V.15.5, 43.1, VIII.23.16, X.61.22, 76.2, and in all cases the mah├бс╕е should be interpr. as adverbial, though the less punctilious тАЬfor great wealthтАЭ probably captures the intended sense just as well.

The tr. of div├нtmate also needs to be revised. I now tentatively accept the analysis of div├нt- and its deriv. div├нtmant- as div-├нt-, a root noun cmpd containing the root тИЪi тАШgo, comeтАЩ. The word is rendered inconsistently in the published translation, as тАШheavenboundтАЩ in I.26.2, тАШheavenlyтАЩ here and X.76.6 (though adjacent div├нt- is tr. тАШheavenboundтАЩ), and тАШheaven-brightтАЩ in V.79.1. This inconsistency reflects the weakness of both standard analyses of this formation, either as an -it-stem with a marginal suffix or as a cmpd. Neither explan. is particularly compelling. For the former, see, e.g., AiG II.2.322, Renou EVP 3.78-79 [ad V.79.1]; for the latter, e.g., Thieme (ZDMG 1961.100 = KlSch 176), AiG II.2.935 (Nachtr.), EWA s.v. dy├бv- (p. 750), and extensive disc. by Scarlatta (44-46). The idea goes back at least to Wackernagel (Sb. Berl.

1918; see Renou op cit.). In this particular case, since the wealth is presumably coming from heaven, not going there, a lit. tr. would be тАЬgreatly for wealth coming from heaven,тАЭ but тАЬтАж for heaven-sent wealthтАЭ would be more idiomatic. The -mantsuffix seems pleonastic+++(=redundant)+++, as AiG II.2.877-78 points out, since the hapax div├нt- and div├нtmant- appear both to be adjectives in the same meaning and are found adjacent to each other in the same case in the one passage in which div├нt- is found (X.76.6).

The reason for -mant- rather than -vant- is likewise unclear (see AiG II.2.882, 891).

English translation:

тАЬYou have spread abroad upon the earth, by your contrivance, the swollen Sindhu when arrested (on its course).тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Sindhu vib─Бlyam vitasth─Бnam : vigatab─Бly─Бvasth─Бm, whose youth was passed, i.e., who was full of water, samp┼лrс╣Зajalam, and vitiс╣гс╣нham─Бnam, stopping or being stopped

Jamison Brereton

And the River Vib─Бl─л, which had spread out upon the earth,
did you hem in, Indra, by your magic power.

Jamison Brereton Notes

vib─Бl─л╠Б- is almost universally taken as the name of (another) river, though the name (and indeed the word) shows up nowhere else. By contrast, in the first ed.

of the dictionary (1872) MonWms. takes it as an adj. vib─Бlya- тАЬpassed beyond a state of youth, in full vigor; swollen (said of a river),тАЭ though in the 2nd ed. (1899) it is simply the fem. river name vib─Бl─л╠Б-. Witzel Got┼Н take it not as a toponym but with the sense тАШmit breiter ├ЦffnungтАЩ. An attributive adjective would certainly be preferable to an unlocatable placename. Although Witzel Got┼Н give no explan. of their interpr., it rests on earlier discussions, whose details can be recovered in EWA (s.v.). EWA considers it the name of a river (produced from the confluence of the Vip─Бs and the ┼Ъutudr─л), but derived from a word with the same (or similar) sense as Witzel Got┼Н ascribe to it: тАШdessen Ufer weit auseinanderstehenтАЩ, an early MIA word with -b─Бra- representing p─Бr├б- тАШfar shoreтАЩ. See the lit. cited there.

And to this unwed girlтАЩs son, who had been shunned, did Indra of a hundred resolves

This son of the unwed maiden appears to be the same one who was being eaten by ants in IV.19.9 (in the same Indra cycle); see comm. there. These tantalizing snippets are all we know about the story.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe lord of acts, the wise Indra, has borne across (their difficulties), Turva┼Ыas and Yadu, when denied inauguration.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Ap─Бrayat =he enabled to cross; i.e., he made them worthy to be inaugurated or crowned which they were not at first, as the text implies by asn─Бt─Бrau, not bathers; allusion is to their exclusion from the succession in favour of the young son Puru by their father Yay─Бti

Jamison Brereton

And these two, Turva┼Ыa and Yadu, who could not swim, did the lord of powers,
the knowing Indra, bring to the far shore.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Witzel Got┼Н render asn─Бt─Б╠Бr─Б as тАЬohne dass sie untertauchen,тАЭ flg. Tichy (Nom.Ag.

107). It seems to me to be pushing the syntax to render a negated agent noun as the equivalent of negative purpose clause (though in her comment Tichy simply says that itтАЩs тАЬgleichzeitig,тАЭ presumably with the time of the main verb), though it is also the case that we donтАЩt know much if anything about swimming in ancient India.

English translation:

тАЬYou have slain at once those two ─Аryas, Arс╣Зa and Citraratha, (dwellig) on the opposite (bank) of the Sarayu.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Those two ─Аryas: ─Бry─Б = ─Бry─Бbhim─Бnau, ─Бryatvabhim─Бninau, presuming on their dignity as ─Бryas, and being without any faith or devotion

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬSlayer of Vс╣Ыtra you have restored the (one who was) blind, the (other who was) lame, both abandoned by their kin); (it is not possible) to exceed the happiness what is given by you.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Blind and lame: in an earlier passage, blindness and lameness were attributed to one person n, Par─Бvс╣Ыja (son of Agru); here, the dual jahit─Б (for jahitau) and dva (for dvau), the two are used

Jamison Brereton

You led along the two that had been abandoned, the blind man and the lame, o Vr╠еtra-smasher:
that favor of yours is not to be equaled.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The blind man and the lame one also figure in IV.19.9, along with the son of the unmarried woman; see vs. 16 above. The blind and the lame form a pair elsewhere in the RV, e.g., I.112.8; II.13.12, 15.7; VIII.79.3.

The infinitival phrase n├б тАж ├бс╣гс╣нave is rendered in the published translation тАЬnot to be equalled,тАЭ though it lit. means тАЬnot to be reached/attained.тАЭ The lit. tr. implies that no one can actually receive IndraтАЩs favor, but I think the point is rather that favor such as IndraтАЩs cannot be deployed by anyone else (that is, any other deity) – hence the adjustment in the English. On this interpr, see Hoffmann (185). Geldner supplies тАЬwith wordsтАЭ (i.e., тАЬnot to be obtained [with words]тАЭ), presumably meaning that no poet can describe the extent of IndraтАЩs favor.

English translation:

тАЬWhen, indeed, Indra, you excite your vigorous manhood, there is no one at the present time who may resist it.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

And now what masculine deed worthy of Indra you will do, o Indra, that no one shall thwart today.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Note the rare future subjunctive kariс╣гy─Б╠Б(с╕е), otherwise found only in corrupted form in I.165.9; see comm. there, as well as Oldenberg on our passage.

Griffith

Indra, whatever deed of might thou hast this day to execute,
None be there now to hinder it.

Geldner

Und auch jetzt noch, wenn du, Indra, eine indraw├╝rdige Tat tun willst, so vereitelt dir diese heute keiner.

Grassmann

Und welche starke Indrathat du, Indra, noch vollbringen willst, Die hindre heute keiner dir.

English translation:

тАЬDestroyer of foes, may the divine Aryaman distribute your precious wealth; (may) P┼лс╣гa (bestow it), (may), Bhaga (bestow it); may the toothless deity bestow the desired wealth.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

The text has: v─Бmam p┼лс╣г─Б v─Бmam bhago v─Бmam devaс╕е kar┼лс╕╖at─л: the triple repetition of v─Бma, vanan─лyam, dhanam would seem to separate not only Bhaga, but Karu.lat─л from P┼лс╣гan;

Kar┼лс╕╖at─л = kс╣Ыttadanta or adantaka, the broken-toothed, or toothless, this term seems to apply to P┼лс╣гan; the legend: p┼лс╣г─Б prapiс╣гс╣нabh─Бgo adantako hity─Бdi ┼Ыrutiс╣гu (Taittir─лya Saс╣Гhit─Б 2.6.8.5); Viс╣гс╣Зu Pur─Бс╣Зa, 67 has P┼лс╣гan whose teeth were knocked out by V─лrabhadra’s followers at Dakс╣гa’s sacrifice

Jamison Brereton

Let the god Aryaman give everything of value to you, o ─АduriтАФ P┼лс╣гan a valuable, Bhaga a valuable, the gap-toothed god a valuable.

Jamison Brereton Notes

The voc. ─Бdure is a hapax, and there is no agreement about whether it is a PN or an attributive adj. and whether it is addressed to a deity (possibly Indra) or a human (possibly a patron). Nor does it seem likely that any definitive answers can be obtained, given the stark paucity of evidence. I have therefore tr. it as a PN as the line of least resistance, and I think it quite unlikely that it is addressed to Indra: would relatively low-level gods be giving things to Indra, and do gods ever receive, rather than give, v─Бm├б-? I tentatively assume that it is the name of the/a patron.

Although this vs. is not technically a d─Бnastuti, it occupies the position in the hymn where a d─Бnastuti would be found, with mention of the human patron, and in opening out to a range of (mostly minor) gods, the mention of a mortal would not be amiss.

On the hapax k├бr┼лс╕╖at─л see EWA s.v. ## 031 Indra According to Oldenberg the hymn is in tс╣Ыcas, but Geldner asserts that it consists of 3 verse pairs and 3 tс╣Ыcas. Geldner concedes that vss. 1-3 occur as a unit in SV, VS, and AV, but argues that the content and form of the verses speak for a different division: vss. 1-2 are questions, vss. 3-4 both begin with the same word, and vss. 5-6 concern the relation between Indra and S┼лrya. After this verse, again on formal and thematic grounds, he considers the rest tс╣Ыcas. Despite these considerations, OldenbergтАЩs view seems correct. That both 3 and 4 begin with abh├н (used in two different senses) is scarcely remarkable; note the verbal concatenation between tс╣Ыcas in the next hymn, IV.32.3-4.

Moreover, vs. 3 fits more comfortably with the preceding vss.: The question тАЬwith what help?тАЭ (k├бy─Б тАж ┼лt─л╠Б) posed in vs. 1 is answered in vs. 3 with the assertion that Indra will be our тАЬhelper with helpтАЭ (avit─Б╠БтАж ┼лt├нbhiс╕е), a satisfying finale to a tс╣Ыca.

Vss. 5-6 do indeed involve Indra and S┼лrya, but vs. 4 provides the lead-in to IndraтАЩs journey continued in vs. 5.

Griffith

O Watchful One, may Aryaman the God give thee all goodly things.
May Risan, Bhaga, and the God Karulati give all things fair.

Geldner

Alles Gute soll dir, Aduri, der Gott Aryaman geben, Gutes Pusan, Gutes Bhaga, Gutes der zahnl├╝ckige Gott.

Grassmann

Gut f├╝r Gut m├╢ge dir, o aufmerkender, Gott Arjaman geben, Gut auch Puschan, Gut Bhaga, und Gut der Gott mit morschem Zahn.
